< Review>
Was staying down the street at the La Quinta and walked here for some (good) coffee with our pups.  It is an adorable little kiosk that was very busy!  There is no seating so you grab and go but they offer fresh baked bakery items - we had the zucchini nut bread which was divine.  Ordered a Mexican Mocha and a Caramel Latte.  Both were excellent.  The gal making the coffee was super friendly and made our drinks to perfection.  Despite the crowd she was un-phased in there by herself and given her positive attitude nobody was going crazy waiting for their coffee.

I love coffee, great coffee and this place served it up to us.

PS - they had a doggy water bowl out which gave them extra points in my book.</Review>

<date>1403138332583</date>< text>
If you check the other reviews I've left both here on Google as well as on Yelp you'll notice I am almost entirely positive. Normally if I can't leave a good review I don't leave one at all, but the pure laziness of the staff at this place is absolutely infuriating and their horrible customer service deserves a bad review.

I gave a ride to a young patient who, because she was once in the Foster Care system, is on Medi-Cal/State Benefits. Unfortunately, the state is often frustrating to deal with: be it an appointment with a medical doctor or dentist, the initial feedback when checking for her eligibility on the computer is that she is not currently active. I've been with her at half a dozen appointments and this issue arises every time. The solution is for the reception staff to make a phone call to the state office- a number provided right on the benefits card for just such an occasion-and speak directly with an agent. I told this to the receptionist and she refused to make the call, stating that these days the computer tells them all they need to know and there is no need to call ("We just don't do that"). From experiences with other medical appointments, we know better. For some reason there is a glitch with this person's account that is ALWAYS cleared up with a phone call. Sure, it's a pain in the butt to have to talk to a live person instead of typing into the computer, but sometimes it's necessary.

The patient called the number herself from her cell phone. As expected, her eligibility was verified. She took her phone to the receptionist, who was informed that she was indeed eligible and that a letter stating that fact would be faxed by the end of the business day. At the dentist or medical offices, this is always enough. Not here! They told this patient that she will have to be rescheduled because they won't see her until the fax actually arrives. It is my opinion that this decision was made, in large part, due to hurt ego: they'd refused to make the call themselves and insisted that "the computer says you are not eligible and that's what we go by now," which was disproven by a simple phone call made by the patient-a call they should have been willing to make themselves.

This patient moves out of state in a week, and made that fact known. She is on an extreme time crunch and her benefits expire soon. Verbal authorization from the state - with the promise by the state's representative to fax an eligibility letter - has always been enough at other medical offices and should have been sufficient in this case as well. This was a case of very, very poor customer service.

EDIT TO ADDRESS "GINA SMITH'S" REVIEW:

If Gina is a real customer, I'd be surprised.

Gina, this isn't a case in which the computer showed this patient as "eligible."  By the way, less than 5 minutes ago, the Doctor's office called and said they would have their billing agent call in to verify eligibility.  That is EXACTLY what I asked them to do while I was in the office with this patient.  It is ALSO what they told me they don't do (see my "We just don't do that" quote above).  I was annoyed when the receptionist said, "We just don't do that" because at every other appointment that I've attended with this particular person, in which the same problem has been encountered, they "just do that" and everything works out perfectly.  It's sad that it took a bad review on Google and Yelp to get this office to do their job as it should have been done when the patient was sitting in the lobby at her scheduled appointment time (10 minutes early, in fact).</text>

<pics>None< /pics><text>I've been going here as long as I can remember and now take my own kids. Office is very friendly, personable and goes out of their way to accommodate any need you might have. Drs. Taxera and Tollman are both excellent in their ability to diagnose and address conditions of eye health, additionally the office is up to date on the latest equipment and technology used in the optometry field.
About five years ago, Dr. Taxera quickly referred my then 12 yr old daughter to a retinal specialist as significant inflammation was present deep in the eyes. Although it was the weekend, he got us an appointment with the specialist for the very next day, Saturday. I appreciate doctors who take a personal interest to ensure the best care is given to their patients and are willing to seek outside medical resources available to address issues beyond their expertise. Although our daughter is now regularly seen and monitored by specialists, Dr Taxera continues to follow her condition and has seen her at a moments notice in times of concern to determine whether or not an unscheduled follow up appt with the specialist was required.
The OptiMap imagery available in their office is very uncommon for an optometrist to have onsite. In fact, UCSF Opthamology department raved about this new equipment they'd recently obtained to take photos of my daughter's eye condition. Upon entering the room we realized it was an OptiMap machine and stated that she'd had that type of imagery done at our general optometry office. It was that very machine used in Dr Taxera's office that took the original photos showing inflammation at the onset of my daughters eye condition. The specialist was surprised and said is was extremely unusual to find that type of equipment in a general practice, especially since their opthamology department had been waiting for some time to acquire one themselves. Very impressive to know Drs Taxera and Tollman invest in technology that helps them give the best care and diagnosis to their patients. I wouldn't go anywhere else!< /text></record>

<name>Brandon Holland<//name>< Review>
My homeowner's association uses Archon "Protection" at night. I have seen the security guard a few times roaming around and stopping to eyeball me when coming home late at night from work. The parking in my small community is a mess, and it is rare that I am able to find a spot anywhere within a half a mile of my house when coming home from a long day at work or school. Today I parked on the street in front of my house (we don't have driveways, but we have a two car garage which is currently filled). I planned to leave very soon after and move my car to a better spot, but completely forgot in my after-school weariness. Around 12:30am, I heard a diesel truck outside. I opened my front door to find my car already hooked to a tow truck after sitting in front of my garage for 2 hours. In their defense, there is a "No Parking - Fire Lane" sign on every street that spans the curbs along our houses, so my car was technically parked in one of the ever abundant "Fire Lanes" and legally hooked to the tow truck. However, my car was no obstruction or hazard to any potential passersby. The security guard did not bother to knock on my door and ask me politely to move my car like any other decent human being would. Instead, he called his buddy at Roy's Towing to have my car towed immediately without giving me any other notice than a citation on my windshield. I asked him why he didn't ask me to move my car, and he told me that it is apparently too dangerous to knock on the door late at night in our humble gated Simi Valley community. The guard and the tow truck driver seemed to have formed a relationship from conning people in the same way in the past. After paying them an absurd $102 to release my car, the security guard smiled and looked to the truck driver before saying, "come on, let's go get the next one." The next car they grabbed was a few streets over, and the poor couple who owned it had to endure the same fate.

Now, I honestly struggle to believe that this security officer has ever done anything other than call that towing service. I have never felt more safe because of his presence, and I would not expect him to be of any assistance in the event of an actual crime occurring in our community. The rumor around the neighborhood seems to be that both the truck driver and the security guard get a small cut of the cash from these transactions. I could not be more disappointed in the way this man handled the situation and I hope to never cross paths with him or Roy's Towing ever again.<//Review>

<rate>5</rate>< Review>
Interesting architecture,  definitely feels old school.   Not particularly ornate as the Pantages  theatre in Hollywood,  still has an amazing feel of authenticity.

The Los Angeles Ballet performance of The Nutcracker in December was delightful.  From the balcony, we could see the entire stage come to life.  My kids enjoyed the ballet, especially my 10 year old daughter.

The audio was good, with ample sound for a classical performance. We will visit again for a concert.  Parking was about a mile walk, but we enjoyed walking through the historic UCLA campus.< /Review>

I want to point out that while I had a great time at the concert, the staffers at Royce Hall did a relatively terrible job managing the show because while a show is going on, it seems that the ushers let people in as the concert in progress. I understand that this is to let people, who paid for their tickets, in but when it gets to the point that so many people are being let in at 20-30 minute intervals and to the point that the performer himself actually has to stop the concert just to let people take their seats, that just completely ruins the experience for everyone.
